# 🇺🇸 DOES THE US WALK THIS BACK, OR DOES IT BREAK APART?

> The question underneath everything in this document.

## What the Research Says About Countries That Backslid

### Countries That Recovered

| Country | What Happened | How They Recovered | Key Factor |
|---------|--------------|-------------------|------------|
| **Poland** | PiS party gutted judiciary, attacked media (2015-2023) | Opposition coalition won election, began restoring institutions | **Elections held + civil society mobilized** |
| **Brazil** | Bolsonaro attacked media, military, elections (2019-2022) | Broad pro-democracy coalition, 900K activists signed letter, voted him out | **Electoral rules stayed intact** |
| **South Korea** | President attempted military coup (2024) | Legislature impeached and removed him within days | **Strong legislature acted fast** |
| **Zambia** | Authoritarian president undermined democracy | Opposition won election, began reforms | Elections + youth mobilization |
| **Senegal** | Democratic backsliding under incumbent | Opposition coalition won | Civil society pressure |

### Countries That Did NOT Recover

| Country | What Happened | Why It Failed |
|---------|--------------|---------------|
| **Turkey** | Erdogan consolidated after "coup attempt" (2016) | Purged 150K, packed courts, won elections anyway — too late |
| **Hungary** | Orbán rewrote constitution, gerrymandered, captured media | Institutions too hollowed out to fight back |
| **Venezuela** | Chávez/Maduro captured military, courts, elections | Opposition won but military refused to recognize results |
| **Russia** | Putin's gradual consolidation (2000-present) | Each step was small enough to not trigger massive resistance |
| **Peru** | Fujimori ousted, democracy returned, but reforms never happened | Corruption continued, democracy stayed fragile, **collapsed again** |

### The Sobering Statistic

From Prof. Nic Cheeseman (University of Birmingham):
> **90% of democratic "bounce-backs" don't last.** Once democracy is lost, durable recoveries are increasingly rare. Most don't hold for even five consecutive years.

### What Makes Recovery Possible

The research identifies two critical factors:
1. **Civil society stays active and informed** — people know what's being done to their democracy
2. **Political opposition uses smart tactics** — broad coalitions, not just partisan fights

Additional requirements:
- **Elections must remain free and fair** — the single most important factor
- **Legislature retains independence** — can check the executive
- **Timing** — respond to threats early, before institutions are hollowed out
- **Institutional reform after recovery** — you can't just go back to the old system, you have to fix the weaknesses that allowed backsliding

---

## So Where Is the US on This Spectrum?

| Recovery Factor | US Status | Assessment |
|----------------|-----------|------------|
| **Elections still functional?** | ⚠️ For now — but SAVE Act, draft voting EO, gerrymandering | Under active attack |
| **Civil society mobilized?** | ✅ 7 million protested, 9 million expected March 28 | Strongest factor in US's favor |
| **Opposition using smart tactics?** | ⚠️ Mixed — Jeffries strategic but party divided on approach | Learning |
| **Legislature independent?** | ❌ Current Congress is not checking executive | Midterms are the test |
| **Courts holding?** | ⚠️ Winning cases but SCOTUS limiting reach + Trump routing around rulings | Eroding |
| **Responded early enough?** | ❓ That's the question | We're past "early" — we're in it |
| **Military stays out of politics?** | 🔴 National Guard in cities, troops used domestically | Posse Comitatus already violated |

**The US matches the RECOVERY cases in one area:** civil society. The protests are enormous and growing.

**The US matches the FAILURE cases in several areas:** courts being undermined, legislature not independent, executive expanding power, military used domestically.

---

## The Four Realistic Scenarios

### Scenario 1: Democracy Recovers (The Poland/Brazil Path)
**Probability: ~30%**

| What Happens | Timeline |
|-------------|----------|
| Blue wave flips House (and maybe Senate) in Nov 2026 | Nov 2026 |
| Investigations, subpoenas, hearings begin | Jan 2027 |
| Trump's power checked legislatively | 2027 |
| Democrat wins 2028 presidential election | Nov 2028 |
| Institutional reforms — court expansion, voting rights act, anti-corruption | 2029-2030 |
| Democracy stabilized (but scarred) | 2030+ |

**What it requires:** Elections stay free enough to work. Enough turnout to overcome gerrymandering + suppression. New president actually reforms institutions (not just reverts to pre-Trump).

**Historical parallel:** Post-Watergate (1974-1976). Congress investigated, president resigned, reforms passed (War Powers Act, FISA, Church Committee). But those reforms took decades to erode — which is why we're here now.

**Risk:** Per Cheeseman, 90% of democratic bounce-backs don't last. Even if the US recovers, without deep structural reform, another authoritarian could do this again in 10-20 years.

---

### Scenario 2: Soft Authoritarianism / Managed Democracy (The Hungary/Turkey Path)
**Probability: ~35%**

| What Happens | Timeline |
|-------------|----------|
| Dems win House but not Senate, or margins too thin | Nov 2026 |
| Investigations stall, impeachment fails to convict | 2027 |
| Trump serves out full term, SCOTUS continues enabling | 2025-2029 |
| 2028 election happens but under tilted rules (voter suppression, gerrymandering, media capture) | Nov 2028 |
| Vance or Trump-aligned successor wins | 2029 |
| US becomes "managed democracy" — elections exist but outcomes are pre-determined | 2029+ |

**What it looks like:** Elections still happen. There's still a Congress. But the courts are packed, the voting rules are tilted, the media is cowed, and the executive operates with few real checks. Like Hungary today — technically a democracy, functionally not.

**Historical parallel:** Hungary under Orbán (2010-present). Turkey under Erdoğan (2014-present). Russia under Putin (2000-2008, before going fully authoritarian).

**This is the most likely scenario** because it doesn't require anything dramatic — it just requires the current trajectory to continue. No revolution, no civil war, no secession. Just slow institutional death.

---

### Scenario 3: Functional Breakup / "Soft Secession" (The EU-ification of America)
**Probability: ~25%**

| What Happens | Timeline |
|-------------|----------|
| Federal government becomes increasingly dysfunctional | Already happening |
| Blue states form compacts — shared environmental, health, immigration, economic policy | 2026-2028 |
| Red states form their own compacts — gun laws, abortion restrictions, immigration enforcement | 2026-2028 |
| Federal law becomes selectively enforced — some states comply, some don't | 2027+ |
| Two (or more) Americas emerge within the same borders | 2028-2032 |
| Dollar remains common currency, military stays unified, but governance is de facto regional | 2030+ |

**What it looks like:** No one formally secedes. The Constitution still technically applies. But in practice, you live in one of two (or three) Americas depending on what state you're in. Blue states have universal healthcare, climate policy, immigrant protections. Red states have virtually no regulation, open carry everywhere, no reproductive rights. The federal government becomes a shell — like the late Holy Roman Empire ("neither holy, nor Roman, nor an empire").

**This is already happening.** Blue states blocking ICE. Red states blocking federal environmental rules. States with completely different abortion, gun, and voting laws. The question is whether it accelerates to the point where the federal government is irrelevant.

**Historical parallel:** Late Habsburg Empire. Late Holy Roman Empire. The EU itself (which is basically this — shared currency and market, but wildly different governance).

**Key insight from scholars:** This doesn't require anyone to choose it. It happens by default when the center can't hold. "Balkanization requires no conscious choice" — it's what happens when institutions stop functioning across state lines.

---

### Scenario 4: Actual Fracture / Civil Conflict (The Yugoslavia Path)
**Probability: ~10%**

| What Happens | Timeline |
|-------------|----------|
| 2026 or 2028 election results contested | Nov 2026 or 2028 |
| Federal government attempts to enforce result, states refuse | 2027 or 2029 |
| National Guard units face loyalty crisis — state vs. federal orders | — |
| Economic crisis triggers cascading state-level action | — |
| One or more states formally declare independence or refuse federal authority | — |
| Military splits or fragments | — |

**What it looks like:** Not the Civil War of 1861 (two armies facing each other). More like Yugoslavia — irregular conflict, militia violence, political assassinations, refugee flows, with international intervention.

**Why it's less likely:** America lacks the ethnic-geographic sorting that made Yugoslavia's breakup "clean." Every blue state has red rural areas. Every red state has blue cities. You can't draw a line. Also, the US military is unlikely to split along state lines — it's a national institution in a way that Yugoslavia's military was not.

**Why it's not zero:** Political violence is already escalating. ICE is operating as a paramilitary. National Guard is in cities. Militia movements are armed and organized. 20% of Americans support a "national divorce." 66% of Southern Republicans polled in 2021 supported leaving the US. If a contested election meets a military loyalty crisis, all bets are off.

---

## The Honest Assessment

| Scenario | Probability | Requires |
|----------|------------|----------|
| **1. Democracy recovers** | ~30% | Midterm wave + 2028 win + deep structural reform |
| **2. Managed democracy (Hungary model)** | ~35% | Nothing — just continuation of current trajectory |
| **3. Soft breakup (EU-ification)** | ~25% | Continued federal dysfunction + state compacts |
| **4. Actual fracture** | ~10% | Contested election + military crisis + economic collapse |

**The most likely single outcome is #2 — slow slide into managed democracy.** Not because anyone chooses it, but because it's what happens when nothing changes enough.

**The most likely GOOD outcome is #1** — but it requires everything to go right: midterm wave, institutional reform, and a post-Trump president who actually fixes the system instead of just going back to normal.

**The scariest thing about #3** is that it's already underway and nobody has to decide to do it. America is already functioning as two countries in one border. The question is how far it goes.

---

## What This Means for Daniel — The Relocation Question

| Scenario | What It Means for You |
|----------|----------------------|
| **Recovery (#1)** | You could stay, but it takes 4+ years and the damage is real. JC is in the crosshairs NOW. |
| **Managed democracy (#2)** | NJ stays blue, but federal enforcement (ICE) continues regardless. Living in a blue state under a red federal government = constant friction |
| **Soft breakup (#3)** | NJ/Northeast block becomes functionally independent. Livable but unstable. Economic disruption likely. |
| **Fracture (#4)** | You want to be somewhere else entirely. |

**In 3 of 4 scenarios, leaving is the safer choice for your family.** Only in Scenario 1 (full recovery) does staying clearly make sense — and even then, the next 2-4 years are dangerous, especially in Jersey City where ICE is actively operating.

The question isn't really "will the US break apart?" It's "**do you want to wait and find out?**"

Per the Carnegie Endowment: the countries that recovered did so because people acted early. The ones that didn't recover are the ones where people said "it can't happen here" until it already had.

**Sources:** [Carnegie Endowment](https://carnegieendowment.org/research/2025/04/democratic-recovery-after-significant-backsliding-emergent-lessons) | [Our World in Data](https://ourworldindata.org/data-insights/four-countries-that-have-successfully-reversed-democratic-decline-in-recent-years) | [Brennan Center](https://www.brennancenter.org/our-work/analysis-opinion/international-lessons-democratic-backsliding-and-recovery) | [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2026/01/31/nx-s1-5684187/after-backsliding-democracy-often-comes-back-weaker-and-more-fragile) | [Journal of Democracy](https://www.journalofdemocracy.org/news-and-updates/can-democracy-recover-after-autocracy/) | [UCSB](https://news.ucsb.edu/2025/021936/could-america-break-apart-ucsb-expert-explores-possibility) | [Chatham House](https://www.chathamhouse.org/2024/02/could-united-states-be-headed-national-divorce) | [Syracuse University](https://news.syr.edu/2025/10/02/secession-in-the-us-could-it-happen/)

| **BOE conflict** | Verbal confrontation between activist and JC Board of Ed president at protest |
| **Mayor Solomon** | Told CBS: "Get out, never come back" to ICE — not cooperating without warrants |
| **DOJ** | **Sued Governor Sherrill** over her executive order limiting ICE on state property |
| **Assemblymen Bhalla + Brennan** | Pledged to fight ICE in Trenton "in every way possible" |
| **ICE propaganda** | ICE issued statement claiming Feb 20 Trenton enforcement coverage was "false reporting spreading fear" |
| **Heights Hospital ER** | **Closing March 14** — the ER in YOUR neighborhood is shutting down |
| **NJCU layoffs** | 151 employees laid off including 33 professors |

**Your neighborhood:** Heights Hospital ER closing in 10 days. ICE operating in your streets. Youth are organizing. Mayor is fighting. DOJ is suing the governor. This is all happening within blocks of your home.

## 📡 ICE SURVEILLANCE EXPANSION

NPR investigation revealed (March 4):
- ICE spent **$5 million** on Thomson Reuters license plate reader subscription
- Trump admin building **unprecedented database aggregating Americans' personal data** for ICE
- ICE brokered deal with **IRS** — judge found IRS **violated federal tax law** by disclosing addresses of 42,000+ people to ICE
- ICE has signed **1,497 local cooperation agreements** (287(g)) across 39 states
- ICE agents have **shot 14 people** since September — fired into cars in multiple incidents

---

## 🔫 Alvarado ICE Facility Ambush Trial

Trial began for 9 defendants accused of attacking Prairieland ICE Detention Center (Fort Worth) on July 4, 2025:
- Fireworks ignited, buildings/vehicles damaged, officers fired upon
- Alvarado police officer shot in the neck (survived)
- Several defendants face **potential life sentences**
- Trial expected to last 3 weeks

---

## 💰 SAVE ACT — Moving Through Senate

The SAVE Act passed the House (nearly party-line) and is now before the Senate:
- Would require passport or birth certificate to register to vote
- **21 million Americans** don't have ready access to those documents
- Critics call it "potentially the worst voting law ever passed by Congress"
- Judge already blocked Trump's parallel EO doing the same thing

# 📊 HOW MASSIVE IS THE US RESISTANCE? — BY THE NUMBERS

> Compiled March 5, 2026. This is the largest sustained resistance movement in American history.

## PROTESTS — Scale Comparison

| Event | Date | Attendance | Context |
|-------|------|------------|---------|
| **50501 — First protest** | Feb 5, 2025 | 72,000 (67 events, 40 states) | Started as a Reddit post |
| **Hands Off** | Apr 5, 2025 | **5.2 million** (1,200 locations) | First mega-protest |
| **No Kings #1** | Jun 14, 2025 | **~5 million** (2,000 cities) | On Trump's birthday, opposite his military parade |
| **No Kings #2** | Oct 18, 2025 | **~7 million** (2,700 cities) | **Largest single-day protest in US history** |
| **Minnesota General Strike** | Jan 23, 2026 | Statewide | First state general strike in decades |
| **Nationwide General Strike** | Jan 30, 2026 | Millions | Schools, workplaces, businesses shut coast to coast |
| **ICE Out Everywhere** | Jan 31, 2026 | 50,000 in Minneapolis alone (300+ events) | Coalition of 50501 + Women's March |
| **No Kings #3** | **Mar 28, 2026** | Expected **9-12 million** | Organizers say "largest in American history" |

### For Perspective

| Protest Movement | Peak | % of Population |
|-----------------|------|-----------------|
| **Vietnam War protests (1969)** | ~2 million (Moratorium) | 1.0% |
| **Women's March (2017)** | ~4.2 million | 1.3% |
| **George Floyd (2020)** | ~15-26 million (over weeks) | 5-8% |
| **No Kings (Oct 2025)** | **~7 million (single day)** | **2.1%** |
| **No Kings (Mar 2026 projected)** | **9-12 million** | **2.7-3.5%** |
| **3.5% threshold (Harvard)** | ~11.5 million | **Historically, governments cannot survive this** |

**Key stat:** Protests in Trump's second term are **4x more common** than his first term (Harvard Crowd Counting Consortium). And they've spread deeper into Trump country than ever before.

**For perspective:** During Trump's entire first term (4 years), the ACLU filed 434 legal actions. In his second term, they've filed **230+ in just 13 months.** The pace has more than doubled.

## PUTTING IT ALL TOGETHER

| Dimension | Scale | Historical Comparison |
|-----------|-------|----------------------|
| **Street protests** | 7 million (single day), 9-12M expected Mar 28 | Larger than Vietnam, Women's March, approaching George Floyd scale |
| **Legal challenges** | 233+ federal cases, 70% win rate | More than double the pace of Trump 1.0 |
| **State flips** | 27-0 (Dem vs GOP) | Worse for incumbent party than any period since tracking began |
| **Special elections** | Dems +13 over 2024 margins | Stronger signal than pre-2018 blue wave |
| **State legislation** | 80+ policies, 51 laws blocking Trump | Unprecedented state-level firewall |
| **Boycotts** | Multiple coordinated economic actions | Growing but impact hard to measure |
| **Geographic reach** | Protests in more US counties than at any point since 2017 | Resistance has reached deep into Trump country |
| **Organizations** | Dozens of legal/advocacy orgs coordinating | More organized than any previous resistance |

### Is It Enough?

**The 3.5% rule:** Harvard's Erica Chenoweth found that no government has survived sustained nonviolent resistance involving **3.5% of the population** (~11.5 million Americans). The October No Kings protest hit 2.1%. March 28 is projected at 2.7-3.5%. **If they hit 3.5%, history says the government cannot hold.**

**But:** Chenoweth's research covers movements that sustained that level over time — not just one day. The question is whether the resistance can maintain these numbers through the midterms and beyond.

**The honest answer:** This is the largest, most organized, most legally aggressive, most electorally successful resistance movement in American history. It is bigger than the Vietnam antiwar movement, bigger than the civil rights movement's peak protest numbers, and more legally coordinated than anything we've seen. Whether it's *enough* depends entirely on November 2026.

**Sources:** [ACLU](https://www.aclu.org/campaigns-initiatives/aclu-vs-trump) | [ACLU 2025 Report](https://www.aclu.org/publications/aclu-2025-annual-report) | [Lawfare Tracker](https://www.lawfaremedia.org/projects-series/trials-of-the-trump-administration/tracking-trump-administration-litigation) | [Bolts - State Flips](https://boltsmag.org/legislative-elections-results-2025/) | [NBC News - 27-0](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2026-election/democrats-flipped-9-seats-state-legislative-special-elections-trump-rcna261633) | [50501 Movement](https://50501movement.online/) | [Harvard Crowd Counting](https://sites.google.com/view/crowdcountingconsortium) | [No Kings](https://www.nokings.org/) | [Axios](https://www.axios.com/2026/01/19/trump-administration-protests-resistance) | [The Bulwark](https://www.thebulwark.com/p/can-lawsuits-tame-this-rogue-presidency) | [DLCC](https://www.dlcc.org/press/data-download-state-democrats-shattered-records-in-2025-elections/)

# 🔥 THE FULL SPECTRUM OF AMERICAN RESISTANCE — EVERY FRONT

> Compiled March 5, 2026. Beyond the protest numbers and lawsuits documented above, resistance to the Trump administration is happening on **every front of American life** — tech, military, churches, labor, campuses, within the GOP itself, in corporate boardrooms, and in newsrooms. Here is every dimension.

---

## 1. TECH WORKERS & SILICON VALLEY

### The Split: Bosses vs. Workers

The top-level story: **Tech CEOs paid to sit next to Trump at his inauguration. Their workers are in quiet revolt.**

- **69% of Silicon Valley residents voted against Trump** — but their bosses (Zuckerberg, Musk, Bezos, Pichai) attended his inauguration in premium seats
- **75% of Silicon Valley residents** say leading tech companies "have too much power and influence"
- **69%** say they've "lost their moral compass"
- The Silicon Valley Index shows the **top 10% hold 75% of the wealth** while the **bottom half hold less than 1%** — 89 billionaires alongside 145,000 millionaires

### Quiet Rebellion

- **Meta employees** brought tampons and pads back to men's bathrooms after Zuckerberg removed them (they had been provided for transgender/nonbinary employees). Management removed them again. Employees brought them back again.
- **Google workers** marched in downtown San Jose on April 5, 2025 — but unlike Trump 1.0 walkouts where Google's own CEO joined, this time organizers **refused to give full names** for fear of retaliation
- **Corporate crackdowns on dissent**: Companies have fired and laid off organizers. The tighter labor market and AI-driven layoffs make workers more afraid

### Corporate Boycotts (Consumer Side)

| Target | Reason | Impact |
|--------|--------|--------|
| **Tesla** | Musk/DOGE | Stock down **50%** from peak; sales cratering in EU |
| **Amazon** | Bezos/Trump alignment | Planned to show tariff impact on prices — killed after Bezos spoke with Trump |
| **Home Depot** | ICE in parking lots | Activist boycott ongoing |
| **Walmart** | Tariff compliance | Regional revenue losses, but stock held |
| **Palantir** | ICE/surveillance contracts | Targeted by immigrant rights groups |
| **Spotify** | Rogan/DOGE ties | Selective boycott |

### Labor Organizing in Tech

- **CWA, OPEIU, and Teamsters** have launched coordinated campaigns to organize the tech sector
- Research shows participation in **social/ethical activism strongly predicts** engagement in labor organizing
- Despite mass layoffs and AI threats, organizing continues underground

**Sources:** [Fortune](https://fortune.com/2025/04/14/tech-bosses-swing-right-almost-7-in-10-silicon-valley-vote-against-trump/) | [Inc.](https://www.inc.com/bruce-crumley/as-silicon-valley-ceos-fawn-over-trump-their-employees-discreetly-resist/91141690) | [Seattle Times](https://www.seattletimes.com/business/silicon-valley-workers-quietly-protest-big-techs-rightward-shift/) | [Washington Post](https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2025/05/16/silicon-valley-workers-dissent-employment-layoffs-whistleblowers/) | [Jacobin](https://jacobin.com/2025/02/tech-workers-silicon-valley-trump) | [Almanac](https://www.almanacnews.com/regional-politics/2026/03/04/distrust-of-tech-helps-drive-populist-fervor-in-silicon-valley/) | [US News](https://money.usnews.com/investing/articles/these-companies-are-being-boycotted-over-trump-policies)

## 2. MILITARY VETERANS & INTELLIGENCE COMMUNITY

### "Don't Give Up the Ship" — The Video That Shook Washington

In **November 2025**, six Democratic members of Congress — all military veterans or intelligence professionals — released a viral video:

| Lawmaker | Background |
|----------|-----------|
| **Rep. Jason Crow (D-CO)** | Army Ranger, 3 tours |
| **Rep. Chris DeLuzio (D-PA)** | Navy veteran |
| **Rep. Maggie Goodlander (D-NH)** | DOJ national security |
| **Rep. Chrissy Houlahan (D-PA)** | Air Force veteran |
| **Sen. Mark Kelly (D-AZ)** | Navy pilot, astronaut |
| **Sen. Elissa Slotkin (D-MI)** | CIA analyst, 3 tours Iraq |

**The message:** "You can refuse illegal orders. **You must refuse illegal orders.**" They told military and intelligence officials: "This administration is pitting our uniformed military and intelligence community professionals against American citizens." The video ended with: **"Don't give up the ship"** — the famous last words of Navy Captain James Lawrence in the War of 1812.

### Trump's Response

Trump posted on Truth Social: **"SEDITIOUS BEHAVIOR, punishable by DEATH!"** In a second post: "Each one of these traitors to our Country should be ARRESTED AND PUT ON TRIAL."

Defense Secretary Pete Hegseth dismissed it as "Stage 4 TDS."

### DOJ Investigation

- **U.S. Attorney Jeanine Pirro** (DC) contacted all six lawmakers requesting interviews
- DOJ explored **seditious conspiracy charges** against sitting members of Congress
- A **grand jury declined to indict** — the investigation fizzled
- The video remains online and has been viewed **tens of millions of times**

### Why This Matters

This is believed to be the first time **sitting members of Congress with active security clearances** publicly told the military to disobey the Commander-in-Chief's orders. It happened in the context of Trump deploying National Guard to US cities and the growing Iran war.

**Sources:** [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2025/11/20/nx-s1-5615190/trump-democrats-military-video-seditious) | [Fox News](https://www.foxnews.com/politics/democrats-urge-military-members-refuse-illegal-orders-viral-video-hegseth-responds) | [Fox 10 Phoenix](https://www.fox10phoenix.com/news/trump-threatens-mark-kelly-other-democrats-jail-time-over-military-video)

---

## 3. CHURCHES & RELIGIOUS RESISTANCE

### The Largest Church-State Confrontation Since the Civil Rights Era

The Trump administration's decision to **revoke the "sensitive locations" policy** (which had protected churches, schools, and hospitals from ICE operations) triggered a massive religious mobilization.

### Minneapolis — Ground Zero

- **January 22, 2026:** Over **600 clergy** from dozens of faiths — Christians, Buddhists, Jews, Muslims, Indigenous practitioners — packed Westminster Presbyterian Church in Minneapolis
- **January 23, 2026:** Over **100 clergy arrested** at Minneapolis-St. Paul airport while praying and protesting ICE actions
- **February 28, 2026:** Trump administration **charged 30 more people** for the Minnesota church protest at Cities Church in St. Paul

### Clergy Under Fire — Literally

| Incident | Details |
|----------|---------|
| **Rev. Kenny Callaghan** (MCC pastor) | ICE agents **pointed a gun in his face** and handcuffed him in Minneapolis |
| **Pastor David Black** (Presbyterian) | **Shot in the head** with pepper spray projectile outside detention center (Oct 2025) |
| **Rev. Jorge Bautista** (UCC, Alameda CA) | **Struck in the face** by a "pepper round" during protest |
| **Compton, CA** | Border Patrol detained two Latino men **outside a church entrance** during worship |
| **Georgia** | ICE arrested a man **outside a church** while his family was inside during service |

### "Prepare for a New Era of Martyrdom"

Bishop Rob Hirschfeld of the Episcopal Diocese of New Hampshire told clergy to "**prepare for a new era of martyrdom**" and put their wills and affairs in order: "It may be that now is no longer the time for statements, but for us with our bodies to stand between the powers of this world and the most vulnerable."

### Denominations in the Fight

- **U.S. Conference of Catholic Bishops** — rare denunciation of "indiscriminate mass deportation"
- **Pope Leo XIV** — called treatment of US migrants "extremely disrespectful"
- **Quakers, Baptists, Sikhs** — suing over sensitive locations policy
- **Mennonites, Unitarians, Methodists, Buddhists** — active in sanctuary networks
- **New Sanctuary Movement (Philadelphia)** — 90+ people from 30+ congregations
- **Maine clergy** — forming "spiritual shields" outside immigrant businesses targeted by ICE
- **New Orleans interfaith coalition** — know-your-rights trainings, protest organizing

### The Sanctuary Movement 2.0

Churches are functionally **recreating the 1980s Sanctuary Movement** — when congregations harbored Central American refugees. This time it's bigger, more interfaith, and facing a more aggressive federal response.

**Sources:** [Religion News](https://religionnews.com/2026/01/23/inside-the-effort-to-organize-clergy-nationwide-to-resist-ice-minneapolis/) | [Axios](https://www.axios.com/2026/02/10/trump-immigration-faith-leaders-resist) | [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2026/02/11/nx-s1-5711631/religious-leaders-response-to-trumps-immigration-crackdown) | [Al Jazeera](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2026/2/28/trump-administration-charges-30-more-people-for-minnesota-church-protest) | [Rolling Stone](https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-features/trump-ice-immigration-church-state-1235507325/) | [Washington Times](https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2026/mar/3/amid-politics-immigration-war-christian-clergy-see-risk-part-moral/) | [Newsweek](https://www.newsweek.com/philadelphia-clergy-protest-ice-immigration-2055239)

## 4. UNIONS & LABOR

### The NLRB Has Been Gutted

Trump effectively **destroyed the National Labor Relations Board**:
- Fired the NLRB chair before her term ended → board lost quorum
- Issued executive order **stripping collective bargaining rights** from 1 million federal employees (NASA, Patent Office, National Weather Service, and more)
- SpaceX and Amazon **filed lawsuits to declare the NLRB unconstitutional**
- DOGE fired tens of thousands of federal workers, **ignoring union contracts**

### AFL-CIO Response

AFL-CIO President Liz Shuler: "We're seeing **the most unified labor movement we've seen in a long time.**" She said Trump's scorecard is "a fail" — "They're slashing jobs. They're ripping up union contracts. They're cutting services."

### The General Strikes

| Date | Event | Scale |
|------|-------|-------|
| **January 23, 2026** | Minneapolis general strike | **~100,000** — first state general strike in decades |
| **January 30, 2026** | Nationwide general strike | Millions — coast to coast, schools/workplaces/businesses |
| **May 1, 2026 (planned)** | May Day general strike | "No Work, No School, No Shopping" — nationwide coalition |

The Minneapolis general strike was triggered by the murder of Renee Nicole Good during an ICE operation. However, the **Minnesota AFL-CIO refused to officially endorse it**, and national union leadership was accused of limiting action.

### Despite Everything, Unions Are Growing

- **Nearly 500,000 workers unionized in 2025** despite relentless attacks
- **1,406 NLRB elections** held in 2025 — unions won **1,152** (82% win rate)
- **75,000 workers** won representation through these elections
- Unions helped win **reinstatement of ~1,000 workers** at NIOSH in January 2026
- **Protect America's Workforce Act** passed the House with bipartisan support (December 2025) — reverses Trump's anti-bargaining executive order

### The Tension

The biggest story in labor resistance is the **gap between rank-and-file militancy and institutional caution**. Workers want general strikes. Union leadership wants to channel energy into the 2026 elections. This tension defined the Minneapolis response and continues to shape strategy.

**Sources:** [Slate](https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2025/05/unions-donald-trump-2026-election-kilmar-abrego-garcia.html) | [AFL-CIO](https://aflcio.org/press/releases/despite-relentless-attacks-nearly-half-million-workers-unionized-2025) | [EPI](https://www.epi.org/publication/unprecedented-the-trump-nlrbs-attack-on-workers-rights/) | [WSWS](https://www.wsws.org/en/articles/2026/01/16/paiy-j16.html) | [MR Online](https://mronline.org/2026/02/28/is-the-labor-movement-growing-or-shrinking-the-incredible-views-of-the-afl-cio/)

---

## 5. STUDENTS & CAMPUSES

### The Campus Crackdown

Trump issued a **"Compact for Academic Excellence"** — schools could sign for priority federal funding, but it required:
- Restricting student protests
- Eliminating gender-neutral restrooms and identity-based affinity spaces
- Limiting international student enrollment
- Submitting to administration oversight

**Result:** Major universities **rejected it**. Brown, MIT, Dartmouth, UVA, Penn, USC, and Arizona all declined to sign.

### The Chilling Effect

- After immigration authorities **arrested Columbia grad student Mahmoud Khalil** (March 2025), another international student was arrested and a third **fled to Canada**
- Student protests at Columbia dropped sharply after the arrests
- Universities nationwide reported students **self-censoring** for fear of deportation or federal retaliation

### Campus Walkouts

| Date | Event | Scale |
|------|-------|-------|
| **September 2025** | D.C. campus walkouts | Georgetown, Howard, GWU, American University — hundreds walked out to protest Trump's DC military takeover |
| **November 7, 2025** | "Students Rise Up" | **100+ campuses nationwide** — rallies, walkouts, teach-ins |
| **Ongoing** | Monthly actions | Leading to planned **May Day 2026 student strike** |

### Coalition Building

"Students Rise Up" includes: Campus Climate Network, Sunrise Movement, Students for a Democratic Society, Public Citizen, AAUP, Higher Education Labor United, and ~24 other organizations.

**Key demand:** Free and fair education, equitable wages for campus workers, protections for marginalized students, and rejection of the Trump Compact.

**Sources:** [Inside Higher Ed](https://www.insidehighered.com/news/quick-takes/2025/11/04/students-unions-protest-trumps-higher-ed-agenda-friday) | [Waging Nonviolence](https://wagingnonviolence.org/2025/12/student-resistance-to-authoritarianism/) | [Washington Post](https://www.washingtonpost.com/education/2025/09/10/trump-dc-protest-college-students-walkout/) | [Common Dreams](https://www.commondreams.org/news/us-campus-protests) | [Socialist Alternative](https://www.socialistalternative.org/2026/02/27/students-for-a-general-strike/) | [NBC News](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/columbia-university-protests-trump-crackdown-rcna198016)

## 6. REPUBLICAN DEFECTIONS & GOP CRACKS

### Record Retirements

**64 members of Congress** (12 senators, 52 House members) are retiring or running for other office as of March 2026 — **more than 10% of Congress**.

- **37 Republicans** vs. 27 Democrats retiring — the GOP is hemorrhaging members
- **10 House Republicans** running for governor — the most from either party since 1974

| Notable GOP Retiree | Significance |
|---------------------|-------------|
| **Mitch McConnell** | Longest-serving Senate leader, clashed with Trump |
| **Thom Tillis** | Moderate, frustrated with "political theater" |
| **Joni Ernst** | Once a Trump ally, grew distant |
| **Don Bacon** | Swing-district moderate |
| **Marjorie Taylor Greene** | Resigned after **public clash with Trump** over Epstein files |

### Actual Defection Votes

- **Tariffs:** Enough Senate Republicans joined Democrats to pass measures rebuking Trump's global tariffs and higher tariffs on Canada/Brazil
- **ACA Subsidies:** **17 House Republicans** used procedural tactics to force a vote extending Affordable Care Act subsidies — breaking Trump's House winning streak
- **Indiana redistricting:** **21 Republican state senators** joined Democrats to vote against Trump's redistricting push, despite Trump threatening primary challenges
- **Rand Paul:** Criticized Trump's military birthday parade: "The image of military parades is really an image that's foreign to our heritage"

### The Electoral Math

- **Generic ballot:** GOP has trailed since March 2025
- **Polymarket:** **70% chance** Democrats retake the House
- **Internal GOP polling:** Republican members of Congress themselves believe they'll suffer in 2026

**Sources:** [CNN](https://www.cnn.com/2025/12/22/politics/trump-republicans-resistance) | [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2025/09/15/nx-s1-5534254/house-senate-retirement-tracker-2026) | [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2025/12/17/nx-s1-5647318/congress-retirement-2026-house-senate) | [VoteHub](https://votehub.com/2026/02/04/republicans-in-congress-voted-in-lockstep-with-trump-in-2025/) | [Newsweek](https://www.newsweek.com/republicans-look-set-get-wiped-out-2025-2026-opinion-2105842) | [The Conversation](https://theconversation.com/who-thinks-republicans-will-suffer-in-the-2026-midterms-republican-members-of-congress-271285)

## 7. CORPORATE AMERICA — THE SILENT RESISTANCE

### The Story: Privately Furious, Publicly Silent

Most CEOs **despise the tariffs** but refuse to speak out. Yale's Jeffrey Sonnenfeld: "Because of the power of this vindictiveness, CEOs are reluctant to poke the bear."

- The White House maintains a **"loyalty rating" of 500+ companies** — tracking who's supportive
- When polled, ~50% of top CEOs said the **S&P 500 would need to fall 20%** before they'd speak collectively
- ~20% said it would need to fall **30%**

### Trump's Direct Pressure

| Target | What Happened |
|--------|--------------|
| **Amazon** | Planned to display tariff impact on prices — killed after Bezos spoke with Trump |
| **Walmart** | Trump publicly demanded they "eat" tariff costs |
| **Intel** | Trump demanded CEO Lip-Bu Tan resign, accused him of China ties |
| **Goldman Sachs** | Trump told CEO David Solomon to "get himself a new Economist" after warnings about tariffs |

### The Few Who Spoke Out

- **Victor Schwartz** (small wine importer) — became lead plaintiff challenging tariffs, **won at the Supreme Court**. Now receives death threats. Called himself "the last line of defense"
- **Ray Dalio** (Bridgewater) — publicly criticized tariff policy
- **Ken Griffin** (Citadel, GOP megadonor) — criticized Trump's attacks on Federal Reserve independence

### The $134 Billion Question

After the Supreme Court struck down IEEPA tariffs, importers may be due **$134 billion in refunds**. But Trump immediately reimposed tariffs under Section 122 — and CEOs **still** won't speak up.

**Sources:** [Fortune](https://fortune.com/2026/02/23/ceo-despise-trump-tariffs-silent-supreme-court-ruling/) | [CNN](https://www.cnn.com/2026/02/21/business/vos-selections-trump-tariffs-lawsuit-risk-takers) | [NPR](https://www.npr.org/2025/08/14/nx-s1-5501591/trump-corporate-america-capitalism) | [Axios](https://www.axios.com/2025/04/03/ceos-react-trump-tariffs) | [Foreign Policy](https://foreignpolicy.com/2025/03/25/sonnenfeld-ceos-trump-tariffs-business/) | [Chatham House](https://www.chathamhouse.org/2025/09/trumps-policies-and-actions-pose-serious-risks-corporate-america)

## 8. MEDIA & PRESS FREEDOM

### By the Numbers (2025)

| Metric | Number |
|--------|--------|
| **Journalists arrested** | **32** |
| **Journalists assaulted** | **170** (160 by law enforcement) |
| **US World Press Freedom ranking** | **57th out of 180** (worst ever) |
| **Journalists per 100K people (2002)** | 40 |
| **Journalists per 100K people (2025)** | ~8 |

The number of assaults on reporters in 2025 **nearly equals the last three years combined.**

### Major Incidents

| Event | Details |
|-------|---------|
| **FBI raid on WaPo reporter** | Hannah Natanson's home raided, devices seized (January 2026) |
| **Don Lemon arrested** | Former CNN anchor arrested covering Minneapolis protest |
| **Georgia Fort arrested** | Emmy-winning journalist arrested covering protest |
| **Pentagon press restrictions** | Required reporters to have material vetted — most outlets **gave up credentials** rather than comply |
| **NPR/PBS funding cut** | $1.1 billion in public broadcasting funds eliminated |

### Lawsuits Against Media

- **$10 billion defamation suit** against Wall Street Journal
- **Settlements extracted** from ABC and CBS News
- **Suing the New York Times**
- **FCC investigations** opened into ABC, NBC, CBS, and local outlets

### The "Antifa" Memo

A national security memorandum defined **anti-Americanism, anti-capitalism, and anti-Christianity** under the "antifa" label — giving government leeway to prosecute speech. Scholars warn it "pushes the limits of presidential authority by targeting individuals based on their beliefs rather than their actions."

### Journalism Fighting Back

- Federal judges have granted media organizations **many early victories** in lawsuits
- **Reporters Committee for Freedom of the Press** testified before House Judiciary Committee (Feb 2026)
- Most mainstream outlets **refused Pentagon vetting requirements** — and are still breaking stories from off-site
- **Freedom of the Press Foundation** launched an expanded strategic plan for 2025-2026

**Sources:** [CJR](https://www.cjr.org/the_media_today/press-freedom-attacks-2025-arrests-detention-journalists-trump-ice-assault.php) | [Poynter](https://www.poynter.org/reporting-editing/2025/united-states-press-freedom-donald-trump/) | [Democracy Now](https://www.democracynow.org/2026/1/15/trump_free_speech) | [ACLU](https://www.aclu.org/news/free-speech/trumps-attacks-on-press-freedom-escalate-npr-pbs-funding-cuts-explained) | [Milwaukee Independent](https://www.milwaukeeindependent.com/newswire/journalists-face-escalating-threats-2026-trump-intensifies-hostility-toward-free-press/) | [AZ Mirror](https://azmirror.com/2026/01/14/how-trumps-attacks-on-press-freedom-and-dissent-follow-the-authoritarian-playbook/) | [CPJ](https://cpj.org/issue/press-freedom-in-the-us/)

## 🗺️ THE FULL RESISTANCE MAP — SUMMARY

| Front | Key Actors | Scale | Effectiveness |
|-------|-----------|-------|--------------|
| **Street Protests** | 50501, No Kings, Women's March, local orgs | 7M+ single day, approaching 3.5% threshold | High visibility, unclear direct policy impact |
| **Legal** | ACLU, Elias Law, Protect Democracy, state AGs | 233+ cases, 70% win rate | **Most effective front** — blocking/delaying policy |
| **State Legislatures** | Dem legislators, some GOP crossovers | 27-0 flips, 80+ policies, 51 laws | Building long-term firewall |
| **Elections** | Dem candidates, grassroots orgs | +13 overperformance in specials | **Most consequential** — Nov 2026 is everything |
| **Tech Workers** | Rank-and-file, CWA, OPEIU | Quiet rebellion, fear of retaliation | Limited by corporate power dynamics |
| **Military/Veterans** | 6 Dem veteran lawmakers, retired brass | Viral video, millions of views | Symbolic but powerful — DOJ backed down |
| **Churches** | Interfaith coalition, 600+ clergy mobilized | 100+ arrested, sanctuary movement growing | High moral authority, taking real physical risks |
| **Unions** | AFL-CIO, UAW, local unions | 500K new members, general strikes | Tension between rank-and-file militancy and leadership caution |
| **Students** | Students Rise Up, SDS, Sunrise | 100+ campuses, building to May Day 2026 | Growing but facing chilling effect (arrests, deportations) |
| **GOP Defections** | McConnell, Tillis, Ernst, Bacon, 17 House Rs | 64 retirements, tariff/ACA votes | Meaningful on specific votes, but most still vote lockstep |
| **Corporate** | Schwartz, Dalio, Griffin | Almost nonexistent publicly | **Weakest front** — fear of White House "loyalty ratings" |
| **Media** | WaPo, NYT, Reporters Committee, CPJ | 32 arrested, 170 assaulted, still publishing | Fighting hard but under unprecedented attack |

### The Big Picture

**What's working:** Legal challenges (70% win rate), state-level resistance (27-0), electoral overperformance (+13), church moral authority, and the sheer scale of protest.

**What's not working:** Corporate silence, union leadership caution, campus chilling effect, and the media being physically attacked while also losing workforce.

**What will decide it:** November 2026. Every front is building toward the midterms. If Democrats flip the House (70% Polymarket) and possibly the Senate, the resistance wins subpoena power, investigation authority, and the ability to block Trump's agenda. If they don't, the resistance has no institutional lever to pull.
